# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/envoy--1d0ba73a` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/envoy--1d0ba73a$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Generate Troubleshooting Runbook for Envoy Connection Pool Management

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/envoy--1d0ba73a (mirror of envoyproxy/envoy)
**Output:** Write your runbook to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a troubleshooting runbook for Envoy's connection pool management. Envoy's connection pools manage upstream HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, and TCP connections, and are a common source of production issues.

## Scope

Explore the connection pool implementation:
- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc` and `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h`
- `source/common/tcp/conn_pool.cc`
- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.cc` — how pools are managed per cluster

## Required Sections

Your runbook at `/workspace/documentation.md` must include:

### 1. Architecture Overview
- How connection pools are organized (per-cluster, per-thread)
- The lifecycle of a connection in the pool (connecting, active, draining)
- HTTP/1.1 vs HTTP/2 pool differences

### 2. Common Failure Scenarios
Describe at least 4 failure scenarios with:
- **Symptom**: What the operator observes (metrics, logs, errors)
- **Root Cause**: What code path leads to this behavior
- **Diagnostic Steps**: Specific Envoy admin API calls or config checks
- **Fix**: Configuration change or code-level explanation

Scenarios to cover (at minimum):
1. Connection pool exhaustion (pending requests overflow)
2. Upstream connection reset / premature close
3. Circuit breaker triggering unexpectedly
4. HTTP/2 GOAWAY causing request failures

### 3. Diagnostic Commands
- Envoy admin API endpoints useful for diagnosing pool issues (`/clusters`, `/stats`)
- Key metrics: `upstream_cx_*`, `upstream_rq_*`, `circuit_breakers.*`
- How to read Envoy's access logs for connection pool errors

### 4. Configuration Fixes
- `max_connections` and `max_pending_requests` tuning
- `connect_timeout` and `per_connection_buffer_limit_bytes`
- Circuit breaker thresholds

### 5. Code References
- Key source files and functions for each failure mode

## Quality Bar

- Metric names must match actual Envoy stats (verify in source or admin API docs)
- Diagnostic steps must be actionable (specific curl commands to admin API)
- Configuration fixes must reference actual Envoy config field names

40-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive troubleshooting runbook for Envoy's connection pool management at `/workspace/documentation.md`.

## Summary

The runbook includes all required sections:

### ✅ 1. **Architecture Overview**
- Connection pool organization (per-cluster, per-thread)
- Connection lifecycle (Connecting → Ready → Busy → Draining → Closed)
- HTTP/1.1 vs HTTP/2 differences (sequential vs multiplexed)
- Pending request queue management
- Code references with line numbers

### ✅ 2. **Common Failure Scenarios** (4+ detailed scenarios)

1. **Connection Pool Exhaustion** — Pending request overflow
   - Causes: max_pending_requests exceeded, all connections busy
   - Diagnostic: Check `upstream_rq_pending_overflow`, `circuit_breakers.*.rq_pending_open`
   - Fix: Increase circuit breaker limits, add endpoints, tune upstream capacity

2. **Upstream Connection Reset** — Premature close
   - Causes: Upstream resource constraints, connection timeouts, protocol errors
   - Diagnostic: Check `upstream_cx_destroy_remote`, `upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject`
   - Fix: Tune keep-alive parameters, increase connect timeout, cycle connections

3. **Circuit Breaker Triggering** — Unexpected rejections
   - Causes: Limits too low, per-host exhaustion, priority mismatch
   - Diagnostic: Compare `upstream_cx_active` vs limits, check which resource open
   - Fix: Increase limits based on load, enable track_remaining, use runtime override

4. **HTTP/2 GOAWAY Failures** — Graceful close handling
   - Causes: Upstream shutdown, SETTINGS mismatch, connection age limits
   - Diagnostic: Check `upstream_cx_close_notify`, look for "remote goaway" logs
   - Fix: Configure keep-alive timers, recycle connections, implement retry policy

### ✅ 3. **Diagnostic Commands**
- Admin API endpoints

  "content": "# Envoy Connection Pool Management Troubleshooting Runbook\n\n## 1. Architecture Overview\n\n### Connection Pool Organization\n\nEnvoy organizes connection pools hierarchically to manage upstream connections efficiently:\n\n- **Per-Cluster Pools**: Each cluster has connection pools segregated by:\n  - Protocol (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, TCP)\n  - Thread (each worker thread has independent pools)\n  - Resource Priority (DEFAULT or HIGH priority requests)\n\n- **Per-Host Pools**: Within a cluster, pools exist per upstream endpoint to ensure load distribution\n\n- **Thread-Local Architecture**: Pools are thread-local to avoid synchronization overhead. Each worker thread maintains its own set of pools.\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h:56-110` \u2014 `HttpConnPoolImplBase` class\n- `source/common/tcp/conn_pool.h:144-187` \u2014 TCP `ConnPoolImpl` class\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h:66-82` \u2014 Pool allocation methods\n\n### Connection Lifecycle\n\nEach connection in the pool transitions through defined states:\n\n1. **Connecting** \u2014 TCP handshake or TLS negotiation in progress\n2. **Ready** \u2014 Connection established, can accept new streams\n3. **Busy** \u2014 All stream slots are occupied (HTTP/2 multiplexed streams)\n4. **Draining** \u2014 No new streams accepted, waiting for active streams to complete\n5. **Closed** \u2014 Connection destroyed\n\n**Transition Logic**:\n- `Connecting` \u2192 `Ready` once connection succeeds (or fails)\n- `Ready` \u2192 `Busy` when max concurrent streams reached (HTTP/2 only)\n- `Busy` \u2192 `Ready` when a stream completes and capacity becomes available\n- `Ready`/`Busy` \u2192 `Draining` on graceful shutdown or connection drain\n- Any state \u2192 `Closed` on connection failure or timeout\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.h:140-156` \u2014 ActiveClient state enum\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:84-120` \u2014 GOAWAY and settings handling\n\n### HTTP/1.1 vs HTTP/2 Pool Differences\n\n**HTTP/1.1 Pools**:\n- One request per connection (sequential processing)\n- Pool size = total concurrent connections\n- Limited by `max_connections` circuit breaker only\n\n**HTTP/2 Pools**:\n- Multiplexed streams on single connection\n- Multiple streams per connection up to `max_concurrent_streams`\n- Limited by both `max_connections` AND stream multiplexing capacity\n- Respects remote SETTINGS frames for max concurrent streams\n- GOAWAY frames trigger graceful connection draining\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:123-157` \u2014 `onSettings()` stream limit adjustment\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121` \u2014 GOAWAY handling\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h:216-245` \u2014 Multiplexed client base\n\n### Pending Request Queue Management\n\nWhen no connections are available, requests queue in `pending_streams_`:\n\n- New requests added to pending queue if no ready connections exist\n- Queue processed when a connection becomes ready (FIFO processing)\n- Queue overflow triggers circuit breaker rejection\n- Pending streams tracked in `upstream_rq_pending_*` metrics\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:71-82` \u2014 `newPendingStream()` implementation\n- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:710-724` \u2014 `purgePendingStreams()` failure handling\n\n---\n\n## 2. Common Failure Scenarios\n\n### Scenario 1: Connection Pool Exhaustion (Pending Request Overflow)\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Requests failing with `overflow` or `no_upstream_host` errors\n- Spike in `cluster.<name>.upstream_rq_pending_overflow` metric\n- `cluster.<name>.circuit_breakers.default.rq_pending_open` > 0\n- High latency or timeouts on downstream clients\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe connection pool has reached its limit of pending requests waiting for a connection. This occurs when:\n1. `max_pending_requests` circuit breaker threshold is exceeded\n2. All `max_connections` are busy/connecting and queue is full\n3. Upstream is slow to accept connections or process requests\n\nThe check happens in `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:226-246`:\n```cpp\nif (parent_.host()->cluster().resourceManager(parent_.priority()).\n      pendingRequests().canCreate() == false) {\n  traffic_stats.upstream_rq_pending_overflow_.inc();\n  return; // Request rejected\n}\n```\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Check pending request overflow metrics:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_rq_pending\n# Look for: upstream_rq_pending_overflow, upstream_rq_pending_active, upstream_rq_pending_total\n```\n\n2. Check circuit breaker status:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | grep -A 20 \"cluster_name\"\n# Look for: \"pending_open\": X (non-zero means breaker is open)\n```\n\n3. Check connection count vs limits:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep \"upstream_cx_\"\n# Compare upstream_cx_total vs circuit_breakers.*.max_connections\n```\n\n4. Review upstream connectivity:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters\n# Check: total_requests_pending (pending streams), total_requests (active)\n```\n\n5. Check logs for connection failures:\n```bash\n# Enable debug logging\n# Look for \"queueing stream due to no available connections\" entries\n```\n\n**Fix**:\n\n1. **Increase circuit breaker limits** in cluster config:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - priority: DEFAULT\n        max_connections: 2000        # Increase from default 1024\n        max_pending_requests: 2000   # Increase from default 1024\n        max_requests: 2000           # Increase from default 1024\n```\n\n2. **Tune upstream capacity**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  # Increase max concurrent streams for HTTP/2\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    max_concurrent_streams: 100\n\n  # Max requests per connection (before cycling connection)\n  max_requests_per_connection: 1000\n```\n\n3. **Improve upstream performance**:\n   - Add more upstream endpoints (horizontal scaling)\n   - Optimize upstream response times\n   - Use connection pooling on upstream side\n\n4. **Reduce downstream request rate** (if appropriate):\n   - Implement rate limiting upstream\n   - Use circuit breaker thresholds to fail-fast\n   - Implement backpressure on downstream client\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 2: Upstream Connection Reset / Premature Close\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Spikes in `upstream_cx_destroy_remote` or `upstream_cx_destroy_local`\n- Requests failing with `RemoteConnectionFailure` or `ConnectionTermination` reset\n- Elevated `upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject` metric\n- Connection-related errors in access logs (5xx, stream reset)\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe upstream is closing connections prematurely or Envoy is not respecting connection keep-alive settings:\n\n1. **Upstream-initiated close**: Remote sends RST or closes TCP socket\n   - Upstream servers are resource-constrained\n   - Upstream has `SO_LINGER` or other TCP settings\n   - Upstream implements strict connection timeouts\n\n2. **Envoy-initiated close**: Envoy closes connection after:\n   - `max_connection_duration` reached\n   - Per-connection request limit (`max_requests_per_connection`) exceeded\n   - Connection idle timeout exceeded\n   - Protocol error on connection\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:151-159` \u2014 Stream reset handling\n- `source/common/tcp/conn_pool.cc:84-112` \u2014 TCP connection event handling\n- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:330-370` \u2014 Connection event callbacks\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Identify connection destruction rate and reason:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_cx_destroy\n# Check: upstream_cx_destroy, upstream_cx_destroy_remote, upstream_cx_destroy_local\n```\n\n2. Check for reset reason distribution:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_rq.*reset\n# Check: upstream_rq_tx_reset (Envoy reset), upstream_rq_rx_reset (upstream reset)\n```\n\n3. Identify if connections are running out of capacity:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_rq_per_cx\n# Histogram showing requests per connection\n```\n\n4. Check Envoy logs for specific reset reasons:\n```bash\n# Enable ENVOY_LOG level for stream reset reasons\n# Look for StreamResetReason enum values\n```\n\n5. Check upstream endpoint health:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | grep -A 30 \"upstream_cluster\" | grep -E \"health|available\"\n```\n\n**Fix**:\n\n1. **Tune connection keep-alive parameters**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  common_http_protocol_options:\n    # TCP-level keep-alive\n    tcp_keepalives:\n      keepalive_probes: 3\n      keepalive_interval: 30s\n      keepalive_time: 60s\n\n    # HTTP keep-alive\n    idle_timeout: 300s        # Default 1h; reduce if upstream is aggressive\n    max_connection_duration:  # Max time before cycling connection\n      seconds: 3600\n\n  # For HTTP/1.1\n  http_protocol_options:\n    allow_absolute_url: false\n\n  # For HTTP/2\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    connection_keepalive:\n      interval: 30s\n      timeout: 10s\n\n  # Cycle connections after N requests\n  max_requests_per_connection: 100000\n```\n\n2. **Increase connection timeout**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  connect_timeout: 10s  # Default 5s; increase if network is slow\n```\n\n3. **Handle upstream resource exhaustion**:\n   - Add more endpoints to spread load\n   - Implement outlier detection to evict problematic endpoints\n   - Monitor upstream CPU/memory via health checks\n\n4. **Configure circuit breaker for graceful failure**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - priority: DEFAULT\n        track_remaining: true  # Fail-fast before exhaustion\n```\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 3: Circuit Breaker Triggering Unexpectedly\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Requests rejected with `overflow` errors\n- `circuit_breakers.<cluster>.<priority>.rq_*_open` or `cx_*_open` > 0\n- Metrics show limits not actually reached\n- Legitimate traffic being rejected\n\n**Root Cause**:\n\n1. **Limits too low for workload**: Circuit breaker thresholds set below actual traffic demand\n2. **Per-host limits exceeded**: Cluster-level limits OK, but per-host limits exceeded\n3. **Priority mismatch**: HIGH priority requests exhausting shared resource pool\n4. **Transient spike**: Brief traffic spike exceeding thresholds\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/upstream/resource_manager_impl.h` \u2014 Resource tracking\n- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:200-202` \u2014 Overflow check\n- `source/common/upstream/upstream_impl.cc:2094-2120` \u2014 Circuit breaker creation\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Check current vs configured limits:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | jq '.cluster_stats[] | select(.name==\"upstream_cluster\")'\n# Look at:\n# - circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_connections\n# - circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_requests\n# - upstream_rq_active (should be < max_requests)\n# - upstream_cx_active (should be < max_connections)\n```\n\n2. Check which resource is exhausted:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep circuit_breakers\n# Identify which _open counter is > 0\n# Possible values: rq_pending_open, cx_open, rq_open\n```\n\n3. Compare remaining capacity to peak traffic:\n```bash\n# Get remaining capacity (if track_remaining is enabled)\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep circuit_breakers.*remaining\n```\n\n4. Check for per-host limits (if configured):\n```yaml\n# Search config for per_host_limits in CircuitBreakers\n```\n\n5. Monitor metrics during traffic spike:\n```bash\n# Continuously poll stats\nwatch -n 1 \"curl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep -E 'upstream_rq_active|upstream_cx_active|circuit_breaker'\"\n```\n\n**Fix**:\n\n1. **Increase circuit breaker limits based on load**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - priority: DEFAULT\n        # Calculate based on: expected_throughput * response_latency_seconds\n        # Example: 10k req/s * 1s response = 10k concurrent requests\n        max_requests: 10000\n        max_connections: 5000\n        max_pending_requests: 5000\n\n      # Separate limits for high-priority traffic\n      - priority: HIGH\n        max_requests: 2000\n        max_connections: 1000\n```\n\n2. **Use runtime override for dynamic tuning** (without reconfig):\n```bash\n# Set runtime flag to override config\ncurl -X POST http://localhost:9901/runtime_modify?circuit_breakers.upstream_cluster.default.max_requests=20000\n```\n\n3. **Enable track_remaining for better observability**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - priority: DEFAULT\n        track_remaining: true  # Exposes *_remaining metrics\n```\n\n4. **Configure per-host limits if appropriate**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  per_host_limits:\n    max_connections: 100\n    max_pending_requests: 100\n```\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 4: HTTP/2 GOAWAY Causing Request Failures\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Requests fail after working initially (then fail consistently)\n- Spikes in `upstream_cx_close_notify` metric\n- Logs show \"remote goaway\" entries\n- All requests to certain endpoint fail (connection-wide)\n- Metrics show `upstream_rq_rx_reset` spike after GOAWAY\n\n**Root Cause**:\n\nRemote server sends HTTP/2 GOAWAY frame, gracefully closing connection:\n\n1. **Upstream graceful shutdown**: Server initiating drain/shutdown\n2. **Upstream SETTINGS frame mismatch**: Remote reduces `max_concurrent_streams` below in-flight requests\n3. **Connection age limit**: Remote enforces connection lifecycle limits\n4. **Protocol violation**: Envoy sent invalid frame, remote closing as error\n5. **Load balancer cycled connection**: Middle proxy closed connection\n\nThe handling is in `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121`:\n```cpp\nvoid MultiplexedActiveClientBase::onGoAway(Http::GoAwayErrorCode error_code) {\n  parent_.host()->cluster().trafficStats()->upstream_cx_close_notify_.inc();\n  if (state() != ActiveClient::State::Draining) {\n    if (codec_client_->numActiveRequests() == 0) {\n      codec_client_->close();  // No active reqs, close immediately\n    } else {\n      // Drain: accept no new streams, close when active complete\n      parent_.transitionActiveClientState(*this, ActiveClient::State::Draining);\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Identify GOAWAY frequency:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_cx_close_notify\n# Spike in this metric means frequent GOAWAY frames\n```\n\n2. Check if problem is upstream-wide or endpoint-specific:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | jq '.cluster_stats[] | select(.name==\"upstream_cluster\") | .host_statuses'\n# Check if all endpoints showing cx_close_notify or just one\n```\n\n3. Check HTTP/2 settings negotiation:\n```bash\n# Enable HTTP/2 debug logging in Envoy\n# Look for \"Adjusting concurrent stream limit\" logs indicating SETTINGS frame received\n```\n\n4. Monitor connection duration:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_cx_length\n# Histogram showing connection lifetimes\n```\n\n5. Check for SETTINGS frame limit reduction:\n```bash\n# Look in Envoy logs for:\n# \"onSettings()\" with maxConcurrentStreams\n```\n\n**Fix**:\n\n1. **Configure connection keep-alive timers** to prevent timeouts:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    connection_keepalive:\n      interval: 30s\n      timeout: 5s\n```\n\n2. **Set aggressive connection recycling** to reduce GOAWAY impact:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  max_requests_per_connection: 1000  # Cycle before remote closes\n  common_http_protocol_options:\n    max_connection_duration:\n      seconds: 3600\n```\n\n3. **Handle SETTINGS frame limits dynamically**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    max_concurrent_streams: 100  # Envoy's max; remote can lower this\n```\n\n4. **Implement automatic connection drain recovery**:\n   - Envoy automatically re-establishes connection for new requests\n   - Configure preconnect to reduce cold-start latency:\n\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  upstream_connection_options:\n    tcp_keepalive: # Ensure TCP keep-alive enabled\n      keepalive_probes: 3\n```\n\n5. **Use retry policy to recover from transient GOAWAY**:\n```yaml\nroute:\n  route:\n    cluster: upstream_cluster\n    retries:\n      num_retries: 3\n      retry_on: \"reset,connect-failure,retriable-4xx\"\n      reset_connect_timeout: true\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Diagnostic Commands\n\n### Key Admin API Endpoints\n\n**Cluster Statistics**:\n```bash\n# List all clusters with current status\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | head -100\n\n# JSON format for programmatic access\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters?format=json | jq '.cluster_stats'\n\n# Filter specific cluster\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | grep -A 50 \"upstream_cluster\"\n```\n\n**Full Statistics Output**:\n```bash\n# Get all stats\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats > /tmp/stats.txt\n\n# Filter to connection pool metrics\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep -E \"upstream_(cx|rq)_\"\n\n# Filter to circuit breaker metrics\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep circuit_breaker\n\n# Filter to specific cluster\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep \"cluster\\.my_cluster\\.\"\n```\n\n**Stats Options**:\n```bash\n# Hide unused stats\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats?usedonly\n\n# Filter with regex (partial match by default)\ncurl -s 'http://localhost:9901/stats?filter=upstream_cx_overflow'\n\n# Full match with anchors\ncurl -s 'http://localhost:9901/stats?filter=^upstream_rq_total$'\n```\n\n### Key Metrics to Monitor\n\n**Connection Metrics**:\n- `upstream_cx_total` \u2014 Total connections opened\n- `upstream_cx_active` \u2014 Current active connections\n- `upstream_cx_overflow` \u2014 Connections rejected due to circuit breaker\n- `upstream_cx_connect_fail` \u2014 Failed connection attempts\n- `upstream_cx_connect_timeout` \u2014 Connections timing out\n- `upstream_cx_destroy` \u2014 Total connections closed\n- `upstream_cx_destroy_remote` \u2014 Remote-initiated closes (GOAWAY, RST)\n- `upstream_cx_destroy_local` \u2014 Envoy-initiated closes\n- `upstream_cx_close_notify` \u2014 Graceful closes (HTTP/2 GOAWAY)\n- `upstream_cx_idle_timeout` \u2014 Connections closed due to inactivity\n- `upstream_cx_max_duration_reached` \u2014 Connections closed due to max_connection_duration\n- `upstream_cx_per_host_overhead` \u2014 Extra connections to same host\n\n**Request Metrics**:\n- `upstream_rq_total` \u2014 Total requests sent\n- `upstream_rq_active` \u2014 Currently active requests\n- `upstream_rq_pending_total` \u2014 Total requests queued\n- `upstream_rq_pending_active` \u2014 Currently pending requests\n- `upstream_rq_pending_overflow` \u2014 Pending requests rejected\n- `upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject` \u2014 Pending requests failed due to connection errors\n- `upstream_rq_*xx` (1xx/2xx/3xx/4xx/5xx) \u2014 Response code distribution\n- `upstream_rq_per_cx` \u2014 Histogram of requests per connection\n\n**Circuit Breaker Metrics**:\n- `circuit_breakers.<cluster>.<priority>.cx_open` \u2014 Connection limit open\n- `circuit_breakers.<cluster>.<priority>.rq_open` \u2014 Request limit open\n- `circuit_breakers.<cluster>.<priority>.rq_pending_open` \u2014 Pending request limit open\n- -e \"\\n--- Request Metrics ---\"\ncurl -s \"$ADMIN_URL/stats\" | grep \"cluster\\.$CLUSTER\\.upstream_rq_\"\n\necho -e \"\\n--- Circuit Breaker Status ---\"\ncurl -s \"$ADMIN_URL/stats\" | grep lb_endpoints:\n          - endpoint:\n              address:\n                socket_address:\n                  address: upstream.example.com\n                  port_value: 80\n```\n\n**HTTP/2 Cluster** (multiplexed):\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: http2_service\n  connect_timeout: 5s\n  type: STRICT_DNS\n\n  # Connection pool sizing (fewer connections, more streams)\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - lb_endpoints:\n          - endpoint:\n              address:\n                socket_address:\n                  address: upstream.example.com\n                  port_value: 443\n```\n\n**TCP Cluster** (generic):\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: tcp_service\n  connect_timeout: 10s  # Longer for non-HTTP\n  type: STRICT_DNS\n\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      -   "content": "# Envoy Connection Pool Management Troubleshooting Runbook\n\n## 1. Architecture Overview\n\n### Connection Pool Organization\n\nEnvoy organizes connection pools hierarchically to manage upstream connections efficiently:\n\n- **Per-Cluster Pools**: Each cluster has connection pools segregated by:\n  - Protocol (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, TCP)\n  - Thread (each worker thread has independent pools)\n  - Resource Priority (DEFAULT or HIGH priority requests)\n\n- **Per-Host Pools**: Within a cluster, pools exist per upstream endpoint to ensure load distribution\n\n- **Thread-Local Architecture**: Pools are thread-local to avoid synchronization overhead. Each worker thread maintains its own set of pools.\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h:56-110` \u2014 `HttpConnPoolImplBase` class\n- `source/common/tcp/conn_pool.h:144-187` \u2014 TCP `ConnPoolImpl` class\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h:66-82` \u2014 Pool allocation methods\n\n### Connection Lifecycle\n\nEach connection in the pool transitions through defined states:\n\n1. **Connecting** \u2014 TCP handshake or TLS negotiation in progress\n2. **Ready** \u2014 Connection established, can accept new streams\n3. **Busy** \u2014 All stream slots are occupied (HTTP/2 multiplexed streams)\n4. **Draining** \u2014 No new streams accepted, waiting for active streams to complete\n5. **Closed** \u2014 Connection destroyed\n\n**Transition Logic**:\n- `Connecting` \u2192 `Ready` once connection succeeds (or fails)\n- `Ready` \u2192 `Busy` when max concurrent streams reached (HTTP/2 only)\n- `Busy` \u2192 `Ready` when a stream completes and capacity becomes available\n- `Ready`/`Busy` \u2192 `Draining` on graceful shutdown or connection drain\n- Any state \u2192 `Closed` on connection failure or timeout\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.h:140-156` \u2014 ActiveClient state enum\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:84-120` \u2014 GOAWAY and settings handling\n\n### HTTP/1.1 vs HTTP/2 Pool Differences\n\n**HTTP/1.1 Pools**:\n- One request per connection (sequential processing)\n- Pool size = total concurrent connections\n- Limited by `max_connections` circuit breaker only\n\n**HTTP/2 Pools**:\n- Multiplexed streams on single connection\n- Multiple streams per connection up to `max_concurrent_streams`\n- Limited by both `max_connections` AND stream multiplexing capacity\n- Respects remote SETTINGS frames for max concurrent streams\n- GOAWAY frames trigger graceful connection draining\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:123-157` \u2014 `onSettings()` stream limit adjustment\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121` \u2014 GOAWAY handling\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h:216-245` \u2014 Multiplexed client base\n\n### Pending Request Queue Management\n\nWhen no connections are available, requests queue in `pending_streams_`:\n\n- New requests added to pending queue if no ready connections exist\n- Queue processed when a connection becomes ready (FIFO processing)\n- Queue overflow triggers circuit breaker rejection\n- Pending streams tracked in `upstream_rq_pending_*` metrics\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:71-82` \u2014 `newPendingStream()` implementation\n- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:710-724` \u2014 `purgePendingStreams()` failure handling\n\n---\n\n## 2. Common Failure Scenarios\n\n### Scenario 1: Connection Pool Exhaustion (Pending Request Overflow)\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Requests failing with `overflow` or `no_upstream_host` errors\n- Spike in `cluster.<name>.upstream_rq_pending_overflow` metric\n- `cluster.<name>.circuit_breakers.default.rq_pending_open` > 0\n- High latency or timeouts on downstream clients\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe connection pool has reached its limit of pending requests waiting for a connection. This occurs when:\n1. `max_pending_requests` circuit breaker threshold is exceeded\n2. All `max_connections` are busy/connecting and queue is full\n3. Upstream is slow to accept connections or process requests\n\nThe check happens in `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:226-246`:\n```cpp\nif (parent_.host()->cluster().resourceManager(parent_.priority()).\n      pendingRequests().canCreate() == false) {\n  traffic_stats.upstream_rq_pending_overflow_.inc();\n  return; // Request rejected\n}\n```\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Check pending request overflow metrics:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_rq_pending\n# Look for: upstream_rq_pending_overflow, upstream_rq_pending_active, upstream_rq_pending_total\n```\n\n2. Check circuit breaker status:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | grep -A 20 \"cluster_name\"\n# Look for: \"pending_open\": X (non-zero means breaker is open)\n```\n\n3. Check connection count vs limits:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep \"upstream_cx_\"\n# Compare upstream_cx_total vs circuit_breakers.*.max_connections\n```\n\n4. Review upstream connectivity:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters\n# Check: total_requests_pending (pending streams), total_requests (active)\n```\n\n5. Check logs for connection failures:\n```bash\n# Enable debug logging\n# Look for \"queueing stream due to no available connections\" entries\n```\n\n**Fix**:\n\n1. **Increase circuit breaker limits** in cluster config:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - priority: DEFAULT\n        max_connections: 2000        # Increase from default 1024\n        max_pending_requests: 2000   # Increase from default 1024\n        max_requests: 2000           # Increase from default 1024\n```\n\n2. **Tune upstream capacity**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  # Increase max concurrent streams for HTTP/2\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    max_concurrent_streams: 100\n\n  # Max requests per connection (before cycling connection)\n  max_requests_per_connection: 1000\n```\n\n3. **Improve upstream performance**:\n   - Add more upstream endpoints (horizontal scaling)\n   - Optimize upstream response times\n   - Use connection pooling on upstream side\n\n4. **Reduce downstream request rate** (if appropriate):\n   - Implement rate limiting upstream\n   - Use circuit breaker thresholds to fail-fast\n   - Implement backpressure on downstream client\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 2: Upstream Connection Reset / Premature Close\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Spikes in `upstream_cx_destroy_remote` or `upstream_cx_destroy_local`\n- Requests failing with `RemoteConnectionFailure` or `ConnectionTermination` reset\n- Elevated `upstream_rq_pending_failure_eject` metric\n- Connection-related errors in access logs (5xx, stream reset)\n\n**Root Cause**:\nThe upstream is closing connections prematurely or Envoy is not respecting connection keep-alive settings:\n\n1. **Upstream-initiated close**: Remote sends RST or closes TCP socket\n   - Upstream servers are resource-constrained\n   - Upstream has `SO_LINGER` or other TCP settings\n   - Upstream implements strict connection timeouts\n\n2. **Envoy-initiated close**: Envoy closes connection after:\n   - `max_connection_duration` reached\n   - Per-connection request limit (`max_requests_per_connection`) exceeded\n   - Connection idle timeout exceeded\n   - Protocol error on connection\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:151-159` \u2014 Stream reset handling\n- `source/common/tcp/conn_pool.cc:84-112` \u2014 TCP connection event handling\n- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:330-370` \u2014 Connection event callbacks\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Identify connection destruction rate and reason:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_cx_destroy\n# Check: upstream_cx_destroy, upstream_cx_destroy_remote, upstream_cx_destroy_local\n```\n\n2. Check for reset reason distribution:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_rq.*reset\n# Check: upstream_rq_tx_reset (Envoy reset), upstream_rq_rx_reset (upstream reset)\n```\n\n3. Identify if connections are running out of capacity:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_rq_per_cx\n# Histogram showing requests per connection\n```\n\n4. Check Envoy logs for specific reset reasons:\n```bash\n# Enable ENVOY_LOG level for stream reset reasons\n# Look for StreamResetReason enum values\n```\n\n5. Check upstream endpoint health:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | grep -A 30 \"upstream_cluster\" | grep -E \"health|available\"\n```\n\n**Fix**:\n\n1. **Tune connection keep-alive parameters**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  common_http_protocol_options:\n    # TCP-level keep-alive\n    tcp_keepalives:\n      keepalive_probes: 3\n      keepalive_interval: 30s\n      keepalive_time: 60s\n\n    # HTTP keep-alive\n    idle_timeout: 300s        # Default 1h; reduce if upstream is aggressive\n    max_connection_duration:  # Max time before cycling connection\n      seconds: 3600\n\n  # For HTTP/1.1\n  http_protocol_options:\n    allow_absolute_url: false\n\n  # For HTTP/2\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    connection_keepalive:\n      interval: 30s\n      timeout: 10s\n\n  # Cycle connections after N requests\n  max_requests_per_connection: 100000\n```\n\n2. **Increase connection timeout**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  connect_timeout: 10s  # Default 5s; increase if network is slow\n```\n\n3. **Handle upstream resource exhaustion**:\n   - Add more endpoints to spread load\n   - Implement outlier detection to evict problematic endpoints\n   - Monitor upstream CPU/memory via health checks\n\n4. **Configure circuit breaker for graceful failure**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - priority: DEFAULT\n        track_remaining: true  # Fail-fast before exhaustion\n```\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 3: Circuit Breaker Triggering Unexpectedly\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Requests rejected with `overflow` errors\n- `circuit_breakers.<cluster>.<priority>.rq_*_open` or `cx_*_open` > 0\n- Metrics show limits not actually reached\n- Legitimate traffic being rejected\n\n**Root Cause**:\n\n1. **Limits too low for workload**: Circuit breaker thresholds set below actual traffic demand\n2. **Per-host limits exceeded**: Cluster-level limits OK, but per-host limits exceeded\n3. **Priority mismatch**: HIGH priority requests exhausting shared resource pool\n4. **Transient spike**: Brief traffic spike exceeding thresholds\n\n**Code References**:\n- `source/common/upstream/resource_manager_impl.h` \u2014 Resource tracking\n- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc:200-202` \u2014 Overflow check\n- `source/common/upstream/upstream_impl.cc:2094-2120` \u2014 Circuit breaker creation\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Check current vs configured limits:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | jq '.cluster_stats[] | select(.name==\"upstream_cluster\")'\n# Look at:\n# - circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_connections\n# - circuit_breakers.thresholds[].max_requests\n# - upstream_rq_active (should be < max_requests)\n# - upstream_cx_active (should be < max_connections)\n```\n\n2. Check which resource is exhausted:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep circuit_breakers\n# Identify which _open counter is > 0\n# Possible values: rq_pending_open, cx_open, rq_open\n```\n\n3. Compare remaining capacity to peak traffic:\n```bash\n# Get remaining capacity (if track_remaining is enabled)\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep circuit_breakers.*remaining\n```\n\n4. Check for per-host limits (if configured):\n```yaml\n# Search config for per_host_limits in CircuitBreakers\n```\n\n5. Monitor metrics during traffic spike:\n```bash\n# Continuously poll stats\nwatch -n 1 \"curl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep -E 'upstream_rq_active|upstream_cx_active|circuit_breaker'\"\n```\n\n**Fix**:\n\n1. **Increase circuit breaker limits based on load**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - priority: DEFAULT\n        # Calculate based on: expected_throughput * response_latency_seconds\n        # Example: 10k req/s * 1s response = 10k concurrent requests\n        max_requests: 10000\n        max_connections: 5000\n        max_pending_requests: 5000\n\n      # Separate limits for high-priority traffic\n      - priority: HIGH\n        max_requests: 2000\n        max_connections: 1000\n```\n\n2. **Use runtime override for dynamic tuning** (without reconfig):\n```bash\n# Set runtime flag to override config\ncurl -X POST http://localhost:9901/runtime_modify?circuit_breakers.upstream_cluster.default.max_requests=20000\n```\n\n3. **Enable track_remaining for better observability**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  circuit_breakers:\n    thresholds:\n      - priority: DEFAULT\n        track_remaining: true  # Exposes *_remaining metrics\n```\n\n4. **Configure per-host limits if appropriate**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  per_host_limits:\n    max_connections: 100\n    max_pending_requests: 100\n```\n\n---\n\n### Scenario 4: HTTP/2 GOAWAY Causing Request Failures\n\n**Symptom**:\n- Requests fail after working initially (then fail consistently)\n- Spikes in `upstream_cx_close_notify` metric\n- Logs show \"remote goaway\" entries\n- All requests to certain endpoint fail (connection-wide)\n- Metrics show `upstream_rq_rx_reset` spike after GOAWAY\n\n**Root Cause**:\n\nRemote server sends HTTP/2 GOAWAY frame, gracefully closing connection:\n\n1. **Upstream graceful shutdown**: Server initiating drain/shutdown\n2. **Upstream SETTINGS frame mismatch**: Remote reduces `max_concurrent_streams` below in-flight requests\n3. **Connection age limit**: Remote enforces connection lifecycle limits\n4. **Protocol violation**: Envoy sent invalid frame, remote closing as error\n5. **Load balancer cycled connection**: Middle proxy closed connection\n\nThe handling is in `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc:111-121`:\n```cpp\nvoid MultiplexedActiveClientBase::onGoAway(Http::GoAwayErrorCode error_code) {\n  parent_.host()->cluster().trafficStats()->upstream_cx_close_notify_.inc();\n  if (state() != ActiveClient::State::Draining) {\n    if (codec_client_->numActiveRequests() == 0) {\n      codec_client_->close();  // No active reqs, close immediately\n    } else {\n      // Drain: accept no new streams, close when active complete\n      parent_.transitionActiveClientState(*this, ActiveClient::State::Draining);\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Identify GOAWAY frequency:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_cx_close_notify\n# Spike in this metric means frequent GOAWAY frames\n```\n\n2. Check if problem is upstream-wide or endpoint-specific:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/clusters | jq '.cluster_stats[] | select(.name==\"upstream_cluster\") | .host_statuses'\n# Check if all endpoints showing cx_close_notify or just one\n```\n\n3. Check HTTP/2 settings negotiation:\n```bash\n# Enable HTTP/2 debug logging in Envoy\n# Look for \"Adjusting concurrent stream limit\" logs indicating SETTINGS frame received\n```\n\n4. Monitor connection duration:\n```bash\ncurl -s http://localhost:9901/stats | grep upstream_cx_length\n# Histogram showing connection lifetimes\n```\n\n5. Check for SETTINGS frame limit reduction:\n```bash\n# Look in Envoy logs for:\n# \"onSettings()\" with maxConcurrentStreams\n```\n\n**Fix**:\n\n1. **Configure connection keep-alive timers** to prevent timeouts:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    connection_keepalive:\n      interval: 30s\n      timeout: 5s\n```\n\n2. **Set aggressive connection recycling** to reduce GOAWAY impact:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  max_requests_per_connection: 1000  # Cycle before remote closes\n  common_http_protocol_options:\n    max_connection_duration:\n      seconds: 3600\n```\n\n3. **Handle SETTINGS frame limits dynamically**:\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  http2_protocol_options:\n    max_concurrent_streams: 100  # Envoy's max; remote can lower this\n```\n\n4. **Implement automatic connection drain recovery**:\n   - Envoy automatically re-establishes connection for new requests\n   - Configure preconnect to reduce cold-start latency:\n\n```yaml\nclusters:\n- name: upstream_cluster\n  upstream_connection_options:\n    tcp_keepalive: # Ensure TCP keep-alive enabled\n      keepalive_probes: 3\n```\n\n5. **Use retry policy to recover from transient GOAWAY**:\n```yaml\nroute:\n  route:\n    cluster: upstream_cluster\n    retries:\n      num_retries: 3\n      retry_on: \"reset,connect-failure,retriable-4xx\"\n      reset_connect_timeout: true\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. # Envoy Connection Pool Management Troubleshooting Runbook

## 1. Architecture Overview

### Connection Pool Organization

Envoy organizes connection pools hierarchically to manage upstream connections efficiently:

- **Per-Cluster Pools**: Each cluster has connection pools segregated by:
  - Protocol (HTTP/1.1, HTTP/2, TCP)
  - Thread (each worker thread has independent pools)
  - Resource Priority (DEFAULT or HIGH priority requests)

- **Per-Host Pools**: Within a cluster, pools exist per upstream endpoint to ensure load distribution

- **Thread-Local Architecture**: Pools are thread-local to avoid synchronization overhead. Each worker thread maintains its own set of pools.

**Code References**:
- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h:56-110` — `HttpConnPoolImplBase` class
- `source/common/tcp/conn_pool.h:144-187` — TCP `ConnPoolImpl` class
- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h:66-82` — Pool allocation methods

### Connection Lifecycle

Each connection in the pool transitions through defined states:

1. **Connecting** — TCP handshake or TLS negotiation in progress
2. **Ready** — Connection established, can accept new streams
3. **Busy** — All stream slots are occupied (HTTP/2 multiplexed streams)
4. **Draining** — No new streams accepted, waiting for active streams to complete
5. **Closed** — Connection destroyed

**Transition Logic**:
- `Connecting` → `Ready` once connection succeeds (or fails)
- `Ready` → `Busy` when max concurrent streams reached (HTTP/2 only)
- `Busy` → `Ready` when a stream completes and capacity becomes available
- `Ready`/`Busy` → `Draining` on graceful shutdown or connection drain
- Any state → `Closed` on connection failure or timeout

**Code References**:
- `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.h:140-156` — ActiveClient state enu
... (truncated)
